Although I've been using allrecipes for over 10 years, I've never found a recipe that I've enjoyed so much that I would join just to rate it, until now! I am 50 plus years old and have been addicted to stuffed cabbage and peppers for most of my life. I have tried hundreds of different recipes. NONE have even come close to this one! My search for the perfect stuffed cabbage or pepper is over! I will never use another recipe. I'm actually getting ready at this very moment to use the filling minus the rice to make homemade ravioli. Thank You Chef John for such a PHENOMINAL RECIPE!

text:
When I asked my boyfriend what types of things he likes to eat are,  after much prodding, the only thing he named was Stuffed Peppers, noting that his mother makes them often.  Later, he said "why don't we just go eat them at my moms?"  Clearly - mom had some good stuffed peppers.

Last night I took a stab at making Stuffed Peppers for the first time ever, for my boyfriend, and used this recipe.  I halved the recipe, and halved 2 large peppers and filled them that way, to make for easier leftover servings.  As I prepared them, my boyfriend stood over me, smirking... and said "your way is a little different."  I could see he was skeptical!!

Presentation wise, these peppers looked the part.  Beautiful.  We sat and ate, and for the first few minutes, didn't speak.  I was getting nervous... I don't think he likes them.  Half way through my plate, he quietly says "These aren't like my moms."  I said "sorry babe..." and before I could finish he exclaimed "THEY"RE BETTER!!!!  THEY ARE SO FREAKIN GOOD!"   And they were!!  As I sit here writing my first review, I'm eating the leftovers.  YUM!!

The only thing, and this may be because I eyeballed halving the recipe, is I wish I made more sauce.  It was delicious and we poured some on extra rice on the side, but there wasn't a lot left for the leftovers.  It was so delicious I'd want extra sauce to pour ridiculous amounts of!  YUM!!  May be different if you do the full recipe, or maybe worth doubling the sauce, or 1 and a half.

text:
We made a double recipe of this, using 8 bell peppers (16 halves). The servings are very generous. I followed the recipe pretty well though I did use less of the cheese as I didn't feel like opening another bag. It got rave reviews from everyone. I loved it, my husband loved it, and the kids loved it. The green peppers and bright red sauce make for pretty contrast, and the savory flavor is wonderful. We had quite a lot left over and the leftovers taste just as good. I would highly recommend making a huge batch, and freezing some. It's cheaper and tastes better than the boxed frozen stuffed peppers.

text:
Probably the best peppers I have EVER eaten! They were fantastic!
I did change it up just a bit because of what I had on hand. I had a 2 pound package of 93% fat free ground beef, so I skipped the sausage. To
mock a spicy sausage flavor, I added some fennel seed, pepper flakes and ground sage to the meat. I used brown rice instead of white rice. For the diced tomatoes I used rotel style tomatoes and drained them. I didn't have any parmesan cheese so what was I going to do? Light bulb moment... those pizza parmesan packets they give you when you order pizza! I have a ton of them so I added about 12 packets of that to the meat. I didn't add the cheese on top until the last 20 minutes and I ended up using mozzarella on top. Served it with some whole grain spaghetti that was tossed with onion, garlic and pepper. TOTALLY delish! I am SO full and I am fighting the urge to go munch on more... the sauce was great too!

text:
I made half of the filling mixture for this recipe and it was plenty for three smallish green peppers (6 halves).  I prepared these early in the day, covered and refrigerated them.  I omitted the pork sausage and used fresh tomatoes.  The recipe is confusing because it instructs you to stir the rice and parmesan into the meat mixture.  Then later instructs you to sprinkle the remaining parmesan (what remaining parmesan?) over the top.  So not knowing how much to put where, I just winged it and used 2 T. in the meat mixture and sprinkled more on top after baking.  I baked these covered for 45 minutes and uncovered for 15 more minutes and my peppers were still crisp tender.  I wouldnâ€™t have wanted to bake them any longer.  This was good and the hint of balsamic vinegar was a nice addition.

text:
I don't think I ever knew real stuffed pepper love until I met these.  Wow.  Other than using red bell peppers I didn't change a thing.  Confusion over when to add the cheese, in the mixture or as a topping, or 1/2 and 1/2.  I added it to the mixture and it was very noticeable and worked out well there.  It would've been difficult to sprinkle on top as there was a LOT of stuffing, so much I piled it as high as I could on each pepper.  Not cooking the meat first seemed stranged to me, but I think this method adds to the flavor and everything cooked to perfect doneness in the time frame given.  Spoon the sauce from the pan on afterwards for flavor and to make it look even tastier.  If you think is good the first night, it's double WOW reheated the next day.

text:
Chef John does it again! I have never made stuffed peppers before, but now I am going to be making these frequently! This recipe is SO tasty! I used whole peppers with the top third cut off. Make sure you really pack the meat/rice mixture into the peppers. This makes it more solid and easier to eat. If you don't they will fall apart when you cut them open to eat. This recipe makes way more meat/rice mixture than you will need, so plan accordingly. UPDATE: You can easily make these healthier by substituting extra lean ground beef (I used 4% fat), turkey hot Italian sausage and brown rice. They still turn out yummy and added bonus: healthy!

text:
this was my favorite stuffed pepper recipe so far, even with substitutions.  I used 1.3lbs ground turkey instead of ground beef and omitted the sausage (because I didn't have time to defrost the sausage I had).  It was plenty of stuffing, though my peppers were pretty small.  Didn't use beef broth, instead added 3/4 cup of the juice I drained from the diced tomatoes.  

Peppers were cooked perfectly not too hard or soft.  Loved the tomato sauce mixture for dipping.  Next time I will try adding the sausage, I think that would take it to another level!  Also, 8 pepper halves do not fit in 1- 9x13, you'll need another small 8x8 to fit all your peppers in.

I served these to company and we all really liked this dish. I followed the recipe as closely as possible and it made just enough stuffing for 6 medium peppers. text:
The time it took and multiple steps before even stuffing the peppers was way too long, a lot of work and the clean up with all the bowls, chopping boards, pots and pans was no party either. I was worried about the Cayenne and Pepper Flakes because of the kids so I went VERY easy on them. When they were done and I tasted a bite, I immediately had a rush of the heat in them. I would never serve to kids. I don't think you need either or the name needs to be changed to something like hot and spicy. If you are good at something you know just stick with it and don't try and get fancy. I learned my lesson and will make my usual next time. For me, nothing special about the taste of this recipe (other than the heat). Save your time and $$$ and stick to your own or one that is much more simple. Thank you for sharing and I'm sorry for being a downer but I read reviews and go by them as I'm sure others do as well. I just wanted to be honest.

text:
As written, this recipe is about 3 stars. First, this makes far too much filling for the 8 bell pepper halves being made.  I ended up only using half of the filling that this recipe made, so I put the remaining filling into a vacuum seal bag and froze it.  The filling otherwise tastes great.  My biggest issue is the cooking instructions.  Next time, I would absolutely cook the filling mixture first in a skillet.  Cooking bell peppers in the oven for 70 minutes renders them mushy.  Cooking the filling in the oven also meant all the grease from the meat dripped out into the already thin marinara sauce, leaving it water and greasy.Next time I will precook the filling in a skillet until almost done, then place the filling in the bell pepper halves and cook at 350 degrees for 25-30 minutes uncovered. Instead of putting the marina mixture on the bottom of the pan, I will keep that separate and place on the peppers when they are served.

text:
This recipe is soooo tasty!  I have made it two times now and I think I have nailed the perfect combination of ingredients (I made a couple modifications from the original).  

My changes

-I use Basmati rice, 2 cups cooked.  
-I throw the garlic in with the onions during their last minute of cooking, so it gets split between the sauce and meat mixture.
-I use tomato sauce, not marinara (which is what this recipe originally called for, anyway)
-I add 1 tsp of worcestershire sauce to the tomato sauce.
-For the meat I only use 1 lb of mild Italian sausage, no ground  beef.
-Because the sausage already has so much flavor, I cut the salt down to 1 tsp.
-I like to use sweet bell peppers; red, orange and yellow.  I find them much more flavorful than green.

Whether you try my changes or stick to the original,  I'm sure you can't go wrong.  Best stuffed peppers ever!

text:
These are the best stuffed peppers I have ever made, and one of the best outcomes for trying a new recipe!!!  A little involved, as there are 3 steps to making--first the rice, next the sauce, and last, the actual stuffing mix.  Not to mention cleaning and cutting the peppers.  It consumed my counter space, so be prepared when you begin.  I made as written, EXCEPT I omitted red pepper flakes and cayenne, and used sweet sausage.  To get a hint of spiciness without the heat, I subbed Rotel MILD for the diced tomatoes.  I was so very tempted to put cilantro in place of the italian parsley, but held myself back!  That's a little 'twist' I'll make next time--perhaps halving the two.  And maybe subbing red wine for the Balsamic vinegar, so many possibilities!  We had leftover peppers tonight, and they were better than they were last night--the balsamic vinegar seems to have mellowed and melded better with time!  I'm freezing the rest, so imagine those will be very delicious, too.  I recommend this highly, and will be my 'go to' for potlucks, as well!

My family loves this recipe.  I use tomato sauce instead of marinara, I use a pound of sausage for 1.5-2 pounds of beef and I double the sauce recipe. I usually buy 6 large peppers to make 12 peppers and then I use any leftover filling to make a small loaf in another pan (also put sauce in the pan.)

I use large peppers and it is a meal in itself, serve with a salad.  For the holidays I am going to try to make the recipe with smaller peppers to make appetizers.

I never made stuffed peppers before but the reviews sounded so great, I decided to give them a try. I'm Sooo glad I did!  These may be my new favorite dish!! I only made a couple changes. I used Johnsonville mild brats in place of hot Italian (didn't want them too spicy for my young kids). I used all 5 brats in the pack. I also added half the canned tomatoes and cut up small pack of variety colored cherry tomatoes I had. I used minute rice also- Anything to save time:) Couldn't find the cheese that was called for so I did a 5 cheese Italian mix. Added half to meat mixture and rest on top. you will have A LOT of filling left. I ended up using more peppers (5 green peppers halved to make 10). I also used  balsamic pomegranate vingear (couldn't find plain one) and I think it only added to the wonderful flavors. Next time I'll try yellow or red peppers too! I will be making this often! ! My Hubby and 2 young kids loved these as well!! Great recipe!!!!!

Really good. I followed the recipe to a tee except I added mozzarella to the top at the end (if you can see my picture, yay!) The braising liquid is very delicious and next time I will try making more of it.

First I must say I do not care for stuffed peppers but my husband does and after 20 years of marriage I figured I should give it a go.  I made the recipe as written and I too must say it makes a huge amount of filling.  I was able to fill 6 large peppers.  I didn't find the recipe difficult or time consuming.  I would suggest reading through the recipe before you start, do all the prep and then you can just breeze through the process.    I still don't care for stuffed peppers but I did like the subtle amount of heat this recipe provides.   My husband liked it and said, "stuffed peppers are always even better left over."   My two teens tried them and didn't care for them but I think its just because I don't make a lot of this type of thing so its not in their pallet.   I gave the extras (after saving one jumbo for hubby) to my elderly parents to provide a meal for them and I know they will like them.   So, I would say it you like stuffed peppers, you will like these and if you've never made them before it's not difficult at all.

OMG were these good.  I used Del Grosso brand marinara sauce (called "Sunday Gravy").  I made these quickly and forgot to add the canned tomatoes.  Also, forgot to buy Parm-Regg cheese so I used just a basic powder parm cheese I had on hand.  Even with these changes the recipe was still fantastic.  My rice never turns out good when made as stated in this recipe.  I add 1.75 c HOT water or chix broth to rice, cook covered on low (or highest simmer setting) for 18 min. Remove from heat, and let rest covered for an add'l 5 min.  Turns out perfect.

This recipe was very easy to make, although I did not have the sausage, I imagine it would bring more depth of flavor. I had 4 large yellow peppers and after stuffing had a lot of mixture leftover. I would think a half cup of uncooked rice would do. But it was fine. I just put the rest of the mixture in the pan with the sauce and the pepper tops. I was also weary of mixing everything with the raw meat- and if I do this again, I may cook the meat just to see how it changes the flavor- with some browned bits, it may be different. I would think you could add anything to this like diced mushrooms or carrots or zucchini or beans. My husband liked it, my one daughter ate the mixture (not the pepper), the other daughter that loves yellow peppers wouldn't touch it (she's only 4 so that explains that) and I enjoyed it, yet felt like it needed something- just not sure what.

text:
As so many before me have noted, these are the best stuffed peppers ever!  I had planned to make stuffed peppers for dinner, but couldn't find my recipe.   Thank goodness I lost it and found this one!!  I modified the recipe out of necessity, as I did not have time to go to the grocery to get the extra ingredients "my new favorite recipe" called for.  I did not have pepper flakes or parsley,  and I did not use  substitutIons.  I prefer lean meats, so I used ground venison in place of the ground beef.  Instead of the sausage, I added another half cup of rice.  I added a tablespoon of olive oil to the meat mixture for added fat.  The tomato sauce was superb and there was plenty to pour over the peppers at serving time.  As the recipe didn't state how to divide the parmesan cheese, I put 2/3 of a cup in the stuffing mixture and 1/3 on the top of the peppers.  I thought the amount of stuffing was perfect for my 4 average to large sized peppers, which I cut in half length wise.   Really push the stuffing in and you'll have them just  nicely heaped.

text:
Amazing! By far, the best stuffed peppers I've ever had. I use ground turkey in place of the beef. I also cook the turkey and sausage before stuffing into the peppers. It cuts down on the baking time and allows me to cook them just until the peppers are perfectly cooked to my liking. ( I like a tiny bit of crunch left in the peppers). I usually use brown rice that I have boiled in reduced sodium chicken broth and it adds a nice flavor. This recipe is more time consuming than any other stuffed pepper recipe I have tried but I promise, it is worth every minute spent in the kitchen!

text:
I had a lot of fun making this. I followed the instructions pretty closely but made done adjustments. 
-i used white cheddar instead of parmesean... Just wanted to make use of what i already had on hand. Cut it into tiny blocks.

- instead of red pepper flakes i used sriracha sauce. Same reason as above. I didn'texactly measure but it was close to 2 tbsp

-i used a whole jar of marinara. I felt like the recipe needsmore moisture to keep the peppers from drying.

-lastly i rotated the dish. halfway through...alll ovens have hot spots. I also "basted" the peppers frequently Sitting the last third of cooking with the tomato sriracha mixture in the pan.


All in all i was happily surprised. Thanks john!

Loved them! I brought it to friends'home and my friend said "My mother taught me how to make stuffed peppers when I was moving away from home. It was one of her signature dishes and I thought the best peppers in the world. These are way superior! May I have the recipe?" 
I did not follow the recipe exactly but would guess they are delicious the way written. Here are the changes I made. I used only sausage because that's all I had, I used brown rice instead of white (Trader Joe's has a quicker cooking brown rice which I love), and I added cooked chard because had some in the refrigerator. I didn't have fresh parsley, so I used Italian seasoning and finally, I used red peppers instead of green because I like a milder taste. They were a 5 star and I will be making them again.

First, I omitted spicy sausage and used regular because I have a picky 4 year old and I thought that the cayenne and the red pepper flakes would provide enough kick (and they did). Second, I omitted the crushed tomatoes altogether and just poured some of the sauce over the peppers before baking. Finally, I did not use beef broth, I rinsed out the tomato sauce can with some water and poured it into the skillet instead. Served with mashed potatoes, with the sauce poured over them. These were the best stuffed peppers I've ever made/had. My husband had two helpings and leftovers tasted just as good the next day.

text:
Fabulous!  I've made this a dozen times and it's 5 Stars as written, but here are my tips...
SAUCE:  It really makes the dish and I now nearly double all ingredients  with the exception of beef broth which I replace with 1 tsp bouillon base (comes in a glass jar).  It's too soupy otherwise. 
VEGETARIANS:  I make half using Gardein Meatless Ground.  I mixed the finished peppers up once and NO ONE could figure out which half was real beef. 
CARB CUTTERS:  I replace half the rice with riced cauliflower and it comes out exactly the same. 
SPEED:  This takes ages to make.  I use steam (microwave) rice and riced cauliflower.  Last night I used already cooked ground beef and turkey mix that I froze a few weeks ago and reduced the cooking time to 70 minutes.  My husband said there was no difference in taste. 
INGREDIENTS:   I use high quality parmesan (Sartori GRATED) and marinara (Rao's).  I also use sweet onions because they taste so good and don't burn my eyes.
YUM!!!

text:
I'm one of those who had never made stuffed peppers without cooking the meat first, and even though it took a while to cook, it was great! My husband ate 3 pepper halfs and literally licked his plate clean! The only changes I made were to use only 1lb of sausage (no beef, adjusted rice accordingly) and I didn't have marinara so I made a quick sauce with canned tomatoes and added the beef broth and balsamic vinegar as directed. The sauce did end up a bit watery, but it didn't stop us from gobbling it up and saving the leftovers! It did make a lot of stuffing. We just piled it on and it was fine.  The peppers were soft, but still had a bite in the time given. I would say if you like a softer pepper then parboil or cook longer, but these were perfect for us. Will become a regular! Thanks!

text:
Best stuffed peppers I ever had!  I had to improvise on a few ingredients but the results were still fabulous. Had no sausage so used only ground beef, had no beef broth so I used a packet of au jus mix I had on hand. Used the green lid type of parmesan cheese since I had no fresh, and used a Google search to find what would replace balsamic vinegar. .. that was apple cider vinegar and brown sugar. The sauce is FANTABULOUS and really makes this dish. I upped the sauce to 1.5x what the recipe calls for,  and next time I'll double or even triple it... it's so delicious spooned over mashed potatoes on the side.  I also added some dried Italian seasoning because I only had a small amount of fresh parsley left.  This makes a TON of stuffing, we ended up using several more green peppers and the last of the banana peppers in our garden. This will definitely be a staple in our rotation. Thanks, Chef John, for the fantastically delicious recipe!

text:
It turned out really well. I added extra garlic and a bit more cayenne and used both parmesan in the meat mixture and Romano on top of it all.
This dish depends in large part on the quality and taste of the sausage. For our taste, we often prefer fairly hot Italian sausage. Many kinds that are labeled as hot have very little hot flavor. I also made this with a sweeter, milder Italian sausage. I added some extra herbs, 6 cloves of garlic and increased the cayenne and red pepper. Really tasty.
NOTE: The preparation time listed for this meal is 30 minutes. Starting with a great deal of chopping, cleaning the peppers, mixing the meat, etc., it took 1 1/2 hours. Then it takes an additional 1 hr and 15 min to bake it. I may be slow, but this meal was a chore. Worth it, though!

text:
One of my fav's of Chef John's. I cook it just often enough to have the recipe memorized. I really don't change much about it at all; why mess with perfection? 
Tonight I had a big can of Tomato puree as opposed to tomato sauce that I normally use so didn't need to thicken the sauce. Otherwise, when I have the tomato sauce I just thicken it with a couple of teaspoons of cornstarch dissolved in a tiny bit of water. (We like a thicker gravy over our stuffed peppers.)  All spices stay the same. 
The combination of spices and the use of two meats make this flavor combo have an all day cooked flavor. I have made this for all my family members including mom and dad and they not only raved, but swore it was the best stuffed pepper they've ever had. I freeze them after the first night's meal and they reheat beautifully. Maybe better? Is that even possible! :)

I just made this for dinner and it was a big hit! I made a couple of small substitutions. First, I used ground turkey instead of ground beef or pork. Secondly I used regular parsley, plus a microwavable sachet of brown rice with black beans for the filling. I noodled a bit with the seasonings, and added some garlic powder and quite a bit of salt and pepper. For the marinara sauce I used a pre-made roasted garlic pasta sauce from a jar. I am guessing I just about doubled the armount of freshly grated Parmesan cheese and it was perfect to keep the turkey from getting too dry. I would definitely make this again - I love you chef John!

text:
Not sure if it made a difference, but after I had the filling and sauce mixed up, I had to stop due to a family emergency, so the 9x13 with the sauce got thrown in the fridge as well as the bowl of the raw rice & meat mixture and it had to sit overnight.  So the next day I brought everything to room temperature, split my peppers and went from there. I doubled the sauce and used rotel instead of plain tomatoes. After I topped the very overtuffed peppers with the cheese, I spooned some of the sauce over the peppers, tented foil over the pan and threw them in the oven for an hour.  Took the foil off and let them go for another half hour.   They got to rest for at least half an hour also before we ate.  Spicy!  Very, very good.  The leftovers were even better!  Will make again for sure.

text:
I made this during the week, doubled the recipe but didn't have sausage so used 2 lb organic ground beef. I didn't have enough fresh parsley so used some dried. I bought a small hunk of Parmigiano Reggiano - yikes, pricey, but grated it and mixed it with some Trader Joe's Parmesan so that there would be enough for the recipe. I used 4 green bell peppers, 2 red, 1 yellow, and one orange, mixed up the colors in two separate casserole dishes. The only canned diced tomato  I had was bigger than what was called for, so drained off some of the juice from 2 cans, and there's plenty of the red sauce.  I watched the video several times, ignored the fancy work with the peppers - just cut them in half and stuffed them - they were big ones. This is the BEST Stuffed Pepper recipe I have ever prepared or eaten, absolutely scrumptious. Thank you Chef John.

Made as directed, I thought this could use a little tweaking. First of all, the filling is rather bland and dry, I think the amount of rice is too much to the ratio of meat/sauce. Add the rice slowly and make sure it doesnâ€™t overtake the meat mixture, I will definitely cut back if I make this again, likely half, this will also help with the issue of having far too much stuffing for the amount of peppers. The sauce mix is delicious! Iâ€™m not sure why this isnâ€™t used as the sauce in the meat/rice mixture. Next time, I will just double the sauce mix and use it in the pan and in the pepper instead of the diced peppers. Also, itâ€™s best to use a low fat meat as the fat canâ€™t be drained off because the meat isnâ€™t precooked before stuffing the peppers. Maybe these tips will help? Recipe is a good starting point though.

text:
Fantastic. Best stuffed pepper recipe ever. I've made it a few times exactly as written, so now I feel comfortable using the recipe as a guide and just "winging it".
Changes I've made to suit my taste: I use 1/2 lb. of spicy italian sausage, italian canned diced tomatoes, and usually have plenty of filling to stuff 5 large peppers, halved lengthwise. I usually add mozzarella to the parmesan that goes on top. 
I spray the foil with Pam so it doesn't stick to the cheese. I add about 5 minutes to the final bake time, since I have so much filling inside of huge peppers - want to be sure everything is cooked thoroughly.
My husband who "hates" green peppers in all forms cannot get enough of this. ;)
Enjoy!

text:
I've made this dish twice now and it's the best stuffed pepper recipe that I have tried.  I made two ingredient changes to make it a tad healthier.  I replaced the rice with quinoa and replaced the Italian sausage with extra lean ground turkey.  I used equal parts of turkey and ground beef.  The last time I made this recipe, I assembled it the day before I baked it.  To cut down on the baking time I decided to boil the peppers in salted water for about 5 minutes, and I also cooked the meat through before I assembled the peppers.  The next day after work I didn't have to bake them as long (heating them through only took about 30 minutes)  and dinner and clean up were a breeze.  Even our picky 10 and 6 year old boys ate every last bit!  Thank you, Chef John!

My dad wanted to know the recipe, but commented that this was a little on the spicy side. Which is fine, I freezed the filling and made more peppers tonight.  Really love this!

text:
I had some large green peppers I needed to use quick so I found this recipe. It turned out really well. The filling was perfectly cooked and the peppers were tender. Of course, I didn't follow the recipe exactly. I had some tomatoes from our garden that we had just stewed with onion and garlic, so I used those for the sauce base and in place of canned diced tomatoes. I didn't use sausage as I wanted to only use things I had on hand. I used less cheese as I needed to share it with another recipe. I mounded the filling up high because I only had 3 peppers that were usable, but it still cooked perfectly. My husband liked it but said it needed salt, which made me realize I forgot to add the salt. If I use stewed tomatoes in place of marinara again, I would probably add a few herbs and more balsamic vinegar. Thank you Chef John! I have a list of other recipes of yours I'm planning to try.

I don't often review recipes, but when my husband gave this a "fantastic" tonight, I felt compelled!  I have made the same stuffed pepper recipe for years, but I will now ditch that one for Chef John's!  I didn't have everything on hand that this recipe called for ... and although I know how much some people hate it when reviewers alter the recipe, I will mention my changes so that others might benefit. country:

text:
Needless to say, I did not follow the recipe exactly because I was working from memory.  After I retrieved the recipe, I went almost exactly as written except for the following.  So, first change was, I cooked sausage and hamburger meat on top of stove.   I made certain to drain it really well because the thought of serving greasy stuffed peppers is  a stomach nightmare.  I used long grain dark rice that cooks in 40 minutes. Only cooked it 20, so as not to make it mushy by overlooking since it would finish in the oven in the marinara sauce.  Added more tomato sauce to the meat mixture around a cup more and also added some olive oil to the meat mixture.  I was afraid that since I had drained the meat, it would be dry, but that wasn't a problem since the peppers are floating in marinara sauce.  I allowed them to float overnight in the refrigerator to allow the flavors to mix.  I used 4 large green peppers cut in two, with holes punched in the bottom. Also cooked it almost 2-hours at 325 in a preheated oven with the roasting pan sitting on a cookie sheet and covered with aluminum foil and parchment paper directly over the peppers.   The cheese was beautifully melted and certainly not stuck on the paper.  It smelled and tasted wonderfully and I got many compliments from the Barnes Family Reunion, in fact, 2 people asked for the recipe.   This recipe takes longer to prepare than specified and longer to bake, too, but it is worth the prize of a rich, delicious stuffed pepper.

text:
This was easily the best stuffed pepper recipe I have ever tried! I put everything together a bit differently due to time constraints but the combination of spices and flavors was outstanding. I cooked the filling and sauce (mixed together) on the stove and then put a little remaining marinara sauce on the bottom of the pan then baked the filling inside the peppers for about 25-30 min. It was fantastic. Peppers were a little undercooked and crunchy but no one seemed to mind. Also I had at least twice as much filling as I needed (to be fair I used 1 1/2 pounds of ground beef) but that worked out great because my kids loved eating the filling just by itself.  My boyfriend requested this dish again so I know it was good! Lol! Will definitely make again!

I've always considered stuffed peppers kind of blah, but these are seriously delicious.  I think it's the sauce, garlic and the bit of hot sausage that makes the flavor great.  My family doesn't love green peppers so I used a mix of red, yellow & orange but otherwise followed the ingredients to a tee. Great recipe, thank you!

text:
This recipe made the best stuffed peppers I've ever had. Even my husband the picky eater loved them. They were even better the next day. The combination of beef and hot Italian sausage is perfect and the balsamic vinegar adds a nice flavor to the sauce. The only modifications that I made to this recipe were to stuff the peppers whole and divide the sauce (about half on the bottom of the pan and then the other half on top of the peppers). If you stuff whole peppers, you will need to increase cooking time accordingly. Mine took around an hour and 20 minutes but were well worth the wait!

text:
Excellent. I cooked Italian hot sausage earlier in the day and then cut into small pieces for this recipe. I did not use ground beef. I also did not use the cayenne or red pepper flakes as the sausage was hot enough. Nor did I use the beef broth but added a couple tablespoons of the marinara sauce to bring the stuffing all together. And did not use 10oz can tomatoes but one big fresh tomato cut in pieces.  Lastly, I did not use Parmesan but feta instead. Since everything was already cooked I baked it for 30 minutes covered and then 15 minutes uncovered. The peppers (used red and orange, not green) were perfect, not soggy, and not too firm,  but nice and tender. Definitely a great recipe!

text:
I don't know what it is, but I absolutely LOVE this recipe! It is so tasty! I have followed it "as is" and I have also tried it with a couple of revisions. Let me just say that there are NO revisions necessary. It is just perfect the way it is! I really believe that those who absolutely hated this recipe, must have done something wrong. I really don't see how you could not like it or how it could possibly be too salty. Like many other reviewers said, it is great with green bell peppers, but I also really like it with orange and red, maybe even a little more.  It is also true that this dish is even better the next day. The last time I made it, I cooked it fully, put it in the refrigerator until the following evening after work, and stuck it in the oven to warm it up. It was perfect! I let the parmesan get a little crusty on top and it was devine. I love it! One important thing to remember is the importance of grating your own parmesan cheese. Do not ever use the stuff in the can that we often use in the United States. It is not the same! You must must must must grate your own good quality parmesan. It is worth it. I promise. Mix some of the parmesan into the meat mixture and put more on the top after you stuff the peppers. It is so good! I serve this with homemade garlic mashed potatoes. I thought the rice in the peppers might be too much starch with the mashed potatoes, but it is not. It is perfect and one of my all time favorites.  Thank you for a really good recipe!

I had several ripe green peppers in my garden and decided to make stuffed peppers.  Although I have never made or eaten stuffed peppers, I thought I'd try something new.  This recipe is absolutely delicious!!  I made it according to the recipe.  The spiciness was a nice surprise and pleasing - and the peppers had a marvelous flavor!  I was concerned that I should blanch the peppers before stuffing them, however, there was no need to add that step as they were very tender!  I did bake for them the entire length of time - the full additional 25 minutes.  My peppers were more of a medium size so I had extra meat mixture that I froze for next time!

This recipe is a keeper!!  I can't wait to make it again when my children are home for the weekend!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Although it takes a little more work, the payoff is totally worth it: I pre-cooked the meat, then poured off the fat and rinsed with hot then cool water (with disposal running) to get nearly all of the grease off. This means you could use less expensive hamburger and sausage, though I used 85% lean beef and 50% leaner Italian turkey sausage. It still yielded way more fat than I'd like.  
While I was prepping the ingredients I put my sliced peppers in a 400 F oven and pre-cooked them for about 20 mins, turning halfway through. With the peppers softened, I filled them and continued cooking with the foil cover for about 20 mins and finished off under the broiler a few minutes until cheese lightly browned. Turned out great! The only other change I will make next time is to use less beef broth or maybe omit altogether. The sauce was a little on the watery side.
I am delighted that I had some leftover stuffing that will freeze well, because I want to make these again in a month or so, and all I have to do is precook more peppers. 
Thank you, Chef John!!

This is an excellent recipe, and by browning the meat, the oven time is drastically reduced. I even froze some (raw, with the rice/sausage cooked, of course), and it was delicious 2 months later when heated in the oven. Suffered no ill effects from freezing.

text:
These were very good and this is a lot coming from me since stuffed peppers are not my favorite dish.  I did make some changes, however, and I apologize for that but they ended up to be so good that I thought I would share. I did not have any sausage so I did not use that.  I sauteed in olive oil a half onion and two garlic cloves diced until softened.  I mixed 1 pound meatloaf mix (ground beef, pork, and veal) with 1 egg, 1/4 cup grated parmesan cheese, 1/4 cup seasoned breadcrumbs, some oregano, garlic and onion powder, salt and pepper , the onion/garlic sauteed veggie mix, 1/4 cup shredded mozzerella cheese and 1/4 cup cooked brown rice.  I sliced red, orange and yellow peppers in half  (removed seeds) and stuffed with a handful of the meat mixture.  I coated baking dish with a light amount of olive oil and added the peppers and I put the sauce (followed Chef John's sauce recipe) on top of the peppers and baked at 375 for about 40 minutes.  They were YUMMY!  The meat was very moist and tasty .  The peppers were cooked perfectly and the sauce had a slight touch of sweetness.  The others who ate them went back for seconds and raved over them stating, "these are the best stuffed peppers I have ever had, including my moms when I was growing up and I thought hers were the best."

text:
I've been trying different stuffed pepper recipes for a while now, and with this one, I can stop my search.  It was by far the best.  We all loved it, though I made a few minor changes, most just depending on taste.  The biggest one was I cut down on the spicyness - to me, stuffed peppers shouldn't be a spicy dish.  So I used sweet Italian sausage instead of hot, cut out the cayenne, and just 1/8 tsp of crushed red pepper.  it still had some spice to it, but not too much.  Also used a little more diced tomatoes, and next time might add 4 oz or so of tomato sauce to give it a little more juiciness.  I used 1/4 cut LESS rice, so it would be a better balance of rice to meat.  And finally, I cut back on the parmesan a bit - thought a whole cup was a bit much, and didn't sprinkle any on top.  It came out very flavorful and will definitely be making it again.

text:
For some reason, every time I've made stuffed peppers, I've had an abundunce of "stuffing". The key is omitting some ingredients, most definitely the rice. It's bulky and is not necessary. If you want rice, serve it on the side. I also omitted the sauce and sausage and still had to pack it down. Also, don't worry about putting half of the sauce on the dish under the pepper. It adds nothing and if anything, makes the pepper soggy. Lastly, tear the white pith from inside the pepper and discard. This will give you more space that you will probably need.

text:
I knew that I liked stuffed bell pepper!  I was just waiting for the right recipe to come along. This is the third stuffed bell pepper recipe I have tried and my husband and I love it.  The sauce is truly what makes this dish.  I did add an extra can of diced tomatoes.  During this recipe I also learned how to soften the bell peppers to create the best texture.   I use to blanch the bell peppers in water.  Instead of blanching, I sprayed oil on a pan and on the bell pepper, heated the oven at 350 and placed the bell peppers cavity down on the pan, put it in the oven for 20 minutes.  Will be making this recipe a lot!

I made this precisely as directed -well, except that I used 3 baby bella mushrooms, chopped, instead of ground beef and added some additional seasoning to the sauce (Penzeys Roasted Garlic and Frozen Pizza Seasoning, mostly because I used plain ol' tomato sauce, not marinara, because it's what I had)- and while I wasn't sure about the sauce at first -just by itself, I thought the beef broth and balsamic vinegar just made it weird- but I was amazed how well it worked with the stuffing and the peppers. Ok. These are amazing. Like "go to the store now and make them tonight" amazing. I crave these things like no one's business. And I don't even normally like peppers.

 Tips: 1. Buy 2-3 extra peppers (it makes a lot of filling)  2. Double the sauce. Trust me. It's that good. (plus you'll run out if you don't)  3. Parboil the peppers for about 3 min.- otherwise they'll still be slightly crunchy  4. Use brown rice if you want to make them healthier (you can't even tell)

I made this for my family last winter and they loved it!! I followed the recipe exactly, the only thing I did different was par-boil my peppers, which were yellow, red, and orange as well as the green.
If you are skeptical about the balsamic, don't be it just adds a depth of flavor, which to me takes it to the next level.
Served as is because it was a hearty meal.  
The prep is a bit time consuming so do it on a night when you are able to relax and enjoy putting it together.
I will make this again, in fact I was on this site looking for the recipe  again to make later this week. This is really a tasty meal.
Hope your family enjoys this as much as we did. 
 Sidebar: this recipe had my inner FOODIE singing opera after tasting these peppers!!!

text:
Absolutely delicious with minor changes 
- use double the amount of bell peppers b/c this is a huge amount of stuffing
- can use all ground beef instead of sausage
- can use water instead of beef broth or omit water entirely because it is very wet
- can use basil instead of parsley (what I had on hand)
- also added mushrooms! This helped add some chewy texture to an otherwise mushy albeit delicious dish
2nd time making it, shortened the cooking time by boiling marinara mixture and adding to raw beef to cook it slightly and then cooked 30 minutes in the oven. Mixture is much wetter so will try to do with only half the mixture next time.  Spoon sauce on top of bell peppers.

text:
This recipe was delicious! I have made stuff peppers before, and my fiance thought they were just okau, but he couldn't get enough of this one! It was a late night when I made this, so I changed up the cooking directions to speed up the process. I added the seasonings and cooked the meat in a pan, then drained the excess grease. I then added about 3/4 of the sauce mixture to the meat, and a little bit of plain marinara to thicken it up. Also boiled the peppers for about 5 min to soften them. II stuffed the peppers with the meat/rice/sauce mixture and topped with cheese, then baked for about 20 min. They were still absolutely delicious and cut the cooking time in half!

These really are delicious! My whole family enjoyed them. I followed the recipe except I had no balsamic on hand so did a tablespoon of red wine vinegar with a teaspoon of sugar added to it. I also had to bake mine about 12 minutes longer, but I stuffed mine pretty full so that's probably why. Also, I used regular sausage and omitted most of the red pepper/cayenne, only adding a small pinch, because my kids reject any spicyness outright (I have a 3 year old). Still tons of flavor and will replace my old traditional B.Crocker recipe!! Even had some leftover to freeze for another day!

text:
I mainly followed the recipe w a few changes. One main change added a delicious twist. Instead of having the marinara on the bottom I the pan I ended up doing something different. I had some home made Katalina dressing left over from a previous recipe. In a skillet I added about a cup of chicken stock, cup of Katalina dressing, 3 garlic cloves, 2 tablespoons fresh basil, 1 tbsp of fresh oregano, 1tbsp of pepper flakes, and pepper to taste. I heated it up on the stove until it was reduced to a thicker consistency. In stead of placing it on the bottom of the pan, I scooped 2 tbsp on the top of each stuffed pepper w the cheese. Delicious sweet and spicy twist !

One MAJOR thing though:  like all stuffed peppers, these taste MUCH better if you cook them for a longer time, on lower heat. Loved the combination of seasonings in this recipe. I did modify to make this healthier & they were AMAZING. 

Used 2 lbs of ground chuck & no pork.
Used brown rice
Cooked the beef and drained the grease before mixing with other items.
Used red peppers, cut in half, dropped in boiling water for 5 minutes, drained & then stuffed.

The flavors are mildly spicy. These are the best flavored stuffed peppers I've ever cooked.

Will definitely cook again.

text:
I made this recipe with the ingredients I had on hand, so used brown rice, ground turkey, omitted parsley, and had the cheese optional. 
The red peppers and cayenne pepper called for by the recipe made me think it would make it too spicy, but it wasn't the case at all. There was double the filling for the bell peppers called for (I think 7 bellpeppers at least to use up all the filling), and you would need a bigger pan than a 9x13 to fit everything. I baked the extra filling in a separate pan. For dinner, I served these in bowls and topped it with the tomato sauce and put cheese on top. TIP: I pre-made the filling earlier in the day so assembly was quick when it came time to bake.

text:
I had every intention of making stuffed peppers but the last thing I felt like doing was running to the store to buy the peppers, so I made a gorgeous gravy instead. Cooked the onions in the olive oil, adding the fresh minced garlic during the last minute or two. Scraped that skillet clean and cooked up the ground beef in it. Drained the beef, added a 24-oz. jar of Rao's Homemade marinara and the rest of the ingredients. For the sausage I used two long grillers (what are these called? Longer than a hot dog, like what you might get on a long roll with peppers and onions). I had these already cooked from the day before so I sliced each one in half lengthwise, then sliced each half into thirds lengthwise, then crosswise to make a small dice. Next time I'll try using ground Italian sausage and will cook it with the beef. I used a can of fire-roasted tomatoes (undrained) because I didn't have regular. I had a beef broth liquid concentrate so I dissolved 2 tsp. in a cup of water and added that...and then I added an extra quick squirt of the concentrate. I also doubled the balsamic. No salt or black pepper, but I did use the cayenne and the red pepper flakes as instructed. I covered the pot and let it simmer for an hour to cook down a little. Used this gravy on top of spaghetti squash and topped with Parmesan and the parsley that I forgot to add to the sauce. You've done it again, John! I'll be making this again and again, and I know that the stuffed peppers will also be phenomenal!

This recipe was AWESOME! I was on the hunt for something quick and easy - didn't have a taste for anything in particular and came across this recipe. This is the 3rd recipe I've made from Chef John and my family was very pleased with it. The only mistake that I made which I think was a good one...was that I accidentally added the diced tomatoes into the skillet with the cooked onions and balsamic vinegar - instead of adding the marinara sauce. I let them simmer for a bit and then took them out with a slotted spoon and then correctly added them to the bowl with the ground beef, sausage, etc. WOW! I think the flavor from the balsamic vinegar, beef broth, etc. was AMAZING inside of the stuffed peppers. Obviously - you don't have to make the same mistake that I did but they turned out great and were full of flavor!

text:
This was my first attempt at stuffed bell peppers in quite a while.  I vaguely recall earlier efforts as not being terribly successful.  Still, I bought some beautiful bell peppers and needed a dinner recipe that would feature them.  I tried Chef John's version of stuffed bell peppers, and they were a HUGE hit!  I modified the recipe slightly based on what I had in the cupboard.  I used red and yellow bell peppers rather than green.  I didn't have Italian sausage on hand, so I used 1.3 lbs of ground beef.  To give them a spicy kick, I substituted a can of Rotel for the diced tomatoes, and a small can of chopped green chiles for the Italian parsley.  I didn't have finely grated cheese on hand, but I did have a shredded four cheese blend, so I used that instead.  They were so good, I had one for breakfast and we are looking forward to leftovers tonight!  This recipe will definitely become a frequent favorite for my household!

text:
I made this recipe tonight and it was a big hit.  Normally when I make stuffed peppers I brown the meat before mixing it with the rice.  This way seems so much better.  The filling turned out juicy and I loved the flavor of the sauce.  I did make a few changes.  I used 1 pound of ground turkey instead of Italian sausage and ground beef because no one in my family likes sausage.  Also, I used whatever leftover rice I had in the fridge, it was probably about 1.5 cups cooked.  Also, I had half a jar of marinara and so I used plain canned tomato sauce for the rest and a beef bouillon cube plus 1 cup of water for the beef broth.  I had enough filling to make 5 generously stuffed peppers (I cut the tops off to stuff them instead of cutting them in half).

text:
I just don't know to change my screw up.

This is my first recipe review on any site. I had to debate a little on  whether to rate this a 4 star or a 3 star. In the end I decided to go with the 4 stars because it still was an amazing new take on an old fashion dish that can be a little boring. It was better than the normal, that's for sure.

PERSONAL OPINION: 
The sauce was too greasy for my liking which I explain below.  

The reason I almost went with the 3 stars is because when I've made this dish in the past,   the sauce was mixed in with the hamburger mix and and then stuffed into the pepper. This allowed me the opportunity to drain the excessive oil and fat from the hamburger. In this recipe because it says to pour it into the baking dish, the fat from the meat drains into the sauce. While I know this adds to the flavor of the sauce, it makes for a very heavy and greasy dish.

CHANGES FOR THE NEXT ATTEMPT:

What I will do next time (and what I recommend for anyone here who wants a lighter dish) is prepare the sauce IN step 4 as usual and after letting it cook for a minute,  in step 5, I'll  instead just set it off to the side rather than pouring it into the baking  dish. This way I can still drain the grease after 45 minutes. Then in step 8, I'll  pour the sauce in and let it cook for the last 25 min. I can't imagine it will alter the taste at all but please correct me if I am wrong. A pound of hamburger and 1/4th pound of italian sausa

Loved these! Yes, they're labor intensive and take up a lot of dishes but I absolutely love this recipe.  I use ground chicken or ground turkey when I make them to cut down the calories, and I think that allows the spiciness from the hot sausage to shine as well as the cayenne and crushed red pepper flakes. I recently made them for my "chicken-a-tarian" friend and even without the sausage she loved them, so there are a lot of alternatives you could use while making these to increase/decrease the heat and to make them healthier.

Very good!  This recipe is a bit time consuming but worth the effort and the wait.  For the amateurs, make sure you wash, cut, chop and gather all of your ingredients before you begin. It will make things go much smoother.  I'm not usually a fan of changing recipes on the first try but this one seemed easy enough to adjust.  I doubled the recipe so I could freeze some for another time.  I used the leftover beef broth in place of some of the water to cook the rice.  We're trying to eat healthier so I used brown rice instead of white and turkey in place of the beef.  Even with the adjustments, this was a super delicious meal.

text:
Perfection!  I make my own tomato sauce (bypassing the beef broth part of the recipe here) in the blender with fresh tomatoes, apple cider vinegar, oregano, basil, red pepper, onion and garlic and then just pour that all over the stuffed peppers.  Brown the sausage a bit before putting it in the stuffing, this makes the flavors pop (I use hot sausage).  I also use plenty of shredded Italian cheese to top the peppers, but I don't put that on until the last 10 minutes.  Great as leftovers or frozen.  Love this recipe so much; I have probably made it at least 10 times :)

I made this for my parents tonight as a "thank you" for letting us stay with them until our new apartment is repaired.  Since I'm a vegetarian, I substituted the beef broth with vegetable broth, beef with Quorn Grounds, and the Italian sausage with Lightlife Italian Sausage.  I didn't change anything else and it turned out absolutely fantastic!  My dad was apprehensive at first, but after trying it exclaimed, "My god! This is actually REALLY good!  Wow!  I really like this!  I was skeptical, but wow.  I am in shock.  This is good!"  

This recipe is DEFINITELY a keeper!
